                  </form> a word of well-known meaning [i. e. <hi rend="ital">A devil;</hi> and with the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">the devil, Satan</hi>]: (S, K:) <hi rend="ital">any that is excessively,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inordinately, proud</hi> or <hi rend="ital">corrupt</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unbelieving</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rebellious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">that is insolent and audacious in pride and in acts of rebellion, of mankind,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of the jinn,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">genii,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">of beasts;</hi> (A'Obeyd, S, Msb, K;) as is shown in relation to the first and second of these by what is said in the Kur vi. 112, and ii. 13 and 96: (TA:) the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> is radical, (S, Msb, TA,) the word being of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَيْعَالٌ</foreign>, from <foreign lang="ar">شَطَنَ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) signifying “ he was, or became, distant, or remote, ” (TA,) or signifying “ he was, or became, remote, or far, from the truth, and from the mercy of God; ” (Msb;) as is indicated by the pl. <foreign lang="ar">شَيَاطِينُ</foreign>; [for] the reading of El-Hasan in the Kur xxvi. 210, <foreign lang="ar">الشَّيَاطُونَ</foreign>, is anomalous, [like <foreign lang="ar">بَسَاتُونَ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">بَسَاتِينُ</foreign>,] and is said by Th to be a mistake: (TA:) or, as some say, the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> is augmentative, (S, Msb, TA, *) and the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> is radical, so that the word is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَان</foreign>, (Msb,) from <foreign lang="ar">شَاطَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَشِيطُ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) signifying “ it was, or became, null, void, of no account, ” and the like, and “ it burned, ” or “ became burnt, ” (Msb,) or signifying “ he burned with anger: ” but the former opinion is the more common: (TA:) [in the Kur, the word is always perfectly decl.; and so it is said to be by SM, in art. <foreign lang="ar">شيط</foreign> of the TA; unless used as a proper name: but J says,] if you make it to be of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَيْعَال</foreign> from <foreign lang="ar">تَشَيْطَنَ</foreign> said of a man, [or rather because they say of a man <foreign lang="ar">تشيطن</foreign>,] you make it perfectly decl.; but if you make it to be from <foreign lang="ar">شَيَّطَ</foreign> [“ he burned ” a thing], you make it imperfectly decl., because it is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَان</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also The <hi rend="ital">serpent:</hi> (S, K:) or <hi rend="ital">a certain species of serpents;</hi> (Fr, S, TA;) <hi rend="ital">having a mane, of foul aspect:</hi> or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">a slender, light,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">active, serpent.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Respecting the saying in the Kur [xxxvii. 63], <foreign lang="ar">طَلْعُهَا كَأَنَّهُ رُؤُوسُ الشَّيَاطِينِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Its fruit is as though it were the heads of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شياطين</foreign>], Fr says that there are three ways in which it may be explained: one is, that the <foreign lang="ar">طلع</foreign> is likened to the heads of the <foreign lang="ar">شياطين</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">devils</hi>] in respect of foulness, or ugliness, because these are described as foul, or ugly: (S:) or it is likened to the <hi rend="ital">evil in disposition of the jinn,</hi> because these are imagined as foul, or ugly: Zj says, in explaining it, that one says of a thing deemed foul, or ugly, <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّهُ وَجْهُ شَيْطَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">as though it were the face of a devil</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّهُ رَأْسُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَيْطَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">as though it were the head of a devil</hi>]; for though the <foreign lang="ar">شيطان</foreign> is not seen, he is conceived in the mind as the foulest, or ugliest, of things: (TA:) the second is, that [the meaning is <hi rend="ital">foul,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ugly, serpents;</hi> for] the Arabs apply the name <foreign lang="ar">شيطان</foreign> to <hi rend="ital">a sort of serpents, having a mane, foul,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ugly, in the head and face:</hi> (S, TA: *) the third is, that <hi rend="ital">a certain foul,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ugly, plat is named</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُؤُوسُ الشَّيَاطِينِ</foreign>; (S, TA;) which is expl. in the K only as meaning <hi rend="ital">a certain plant.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَيْطَانُ الفَلَا</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">The devil of the waterless deserts</hi>] means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">thirst.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">شَيْطَانٌ</foreign> signifies also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Any blamable faculty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">power,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">propensity,</hi>] of a man. (Er-Rághib, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">رَكِبَهُ شَيْطَانُهُ</foreign> i. e. <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">His anger got the ascendency over him;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, angry.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">نَزَعَ شَيْطَانَهُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He plucked out his pride.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  Also, [probably as being likened to a serpent,] <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A mark made with a hot iron in the upper part of the haunch of a camel, perpendicularly, upon the thigh, extending to the hock;</hi> (K, TA;) from the “ Tedhkireh ” of Aboo-'Alee; (TA;) likewise called
